  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer1354679533170185030">Tessa is a good girl with a sweet, reliable boyfriend back home. She’s got direction, ambition, and a mother who’s intent on keeping her that way. <br/><br/>But she’s barely moved into her freshman dorm when she runs into Hardin.   <span id="freeText1354679533170185030" style="display:none">Tessa is a good girl with a sweet, reliable boyfriend back home. She’s got direction, ambition, and a mother who’s intent on keeping her that way. <br /><br />But she’s barely moved into her freshman dorm when she runs into Hardin. With his tousled brown hair, cocky British accent, tattoos, and lip ring, Hardin is cute and different from what she’s used to. <br /><br />But he’s also rude—to the point of cruelty, even. For all his attitude, Tessa <i>should</i> hate Hardin. And she does—until she finds herself alone with him in his room. Something about his dark mood grabs her, and when they kiss it ignites within her a passion she’s never known before. <br /><br />He’ll call her beautiful, then insist he isn't the one for her and disappear again and again. Despite the reckless way he treats her, Tessa is compelled to dig deeper and find the real Hardin beneath all his lies. He pushes her away again and again, yet every time she pushes back, he only pulls her in deeper. <br /><br />Tessa already has the perfect boyfriend. So why is she trying so hard to overcome her own hurt pride and Hardin’s prejudice about nice girls like her? <br /><br />Unless…could this be <i>love</i>?<br /><br />Now newly revised and expanded, Anna Todd’s After fanfiction racked up 1 billion reads online and captivated readers across the globe. Experience the Internet’s most talked-about book for yourself!<br /><br />There was the time before Tessa met Hardin, and then there’s everything <b>
  <i>AFTER</i>
</b>... Life will never be the same.</span>

      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_42299840').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_42299840').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_42299840').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/199650-okay-i-must-ask-because-i-don-t-get-it">okay, I must ask because I don;t get it. What does it have to do with One Direction? how did so many people read it and like it? how is it different from all those ya novels?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_199650'><a id="like_count_community_question_199650" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/199650?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">31 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F22557520-after">like</a></span>

<a href="/questions/199650-okay-i-must-ask-because-i-don-t-get-it">6 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/199650-okay-i-must-ask-because-i-don-t-get-it">See all 9 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/18777164-jen"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1505410530i/18777164._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/18777164-jen">Jen</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
     In the fan fiction-reading community, there are stories that are based on the actual person/character, for example, if this story were about Harry St<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
     In the fan fiction-reading community, there are stories that are based on the actual person/character, for example, if this story were about Harry Styles in a boy band, it would be the kind that's actually based on the real-life character. Then, there are AU stories, which stands for "Alternate Universe", i.e., Harry Styles- who is actually a band member in real life- is depicted as a normal college boy instead of an international pop star. This kind of fan fiction style is very popular and common in the One Direction fandom. That's what it has to do with One Direction. It's LOOSELY based on them, therefore if you change the names it's as if you could never tell it was a fan fiction about Harry Styles. <br /> A lot of people read it and did not like it because for one, it is TERRIBLY written. It's almost hard to believe Anna Todd is twenty-five. The plot.. what plot? Another thing that made people dislike it so much is the themes in it. Themes of abuse, drinking, assault, DUI.. The character of "Hardin" isolates, humiliates and intimidates Tessa. He drinks every time something bad happens (He's an ANGRY, jealous drunk.). He has horrible, triggering anger rages and in the author's eyes the only thing that solves these problems are them having sex. Honestly, that's the only bond they have: sex. Hardin beats anyone who looks at Tessa to a pulp. It's a trashy book that romanticizes abuse and drinking. <br /> Keep in mind this is a FANFICTION about a boy band member that appeals to TEENAGE girls. These teenage girls are probably thinking, "Hey, if my man abuses me like this it's okay because he loves me, the sex is great and he just needs to work it out." Anna Todd seems to justify Hardin's behavior by saying that he is that way because his father was abusive towards him during his childhood as well. It's just a sickening book- better you stray far away from it. She's tried to milk this thing out for so much money- I really do hope Harry Styles can find some grounds that he can sue her on. This is just WRONG profit. As trashy as Fifty Shades was, at least E.L James had the decency to realize she was publishing a series about FICTIONAL characters, not a series about a mortified 20 year old band member who's gonna have this TRASH excuse of a book following him his entire career. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_949725273" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/949725273" />
    <a title="Mila Temnyalova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14766949-mila-temnyalova"><img alt="Mila Temnyalova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370720115p2/14766949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/949725273?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mila Temnyalova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mila Temnyalova" href="/user/show/14766949-mila-temnyalova">Mila Temnyalova</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/18455315-after">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer949725273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6551181784704954757">I don't normally read fan fiction on Wattpad. One Direction fanfiction, even less so. But given that this trilogy nearly has one BILLION reads altogether, I thought to myself: this can't be that bad -- after all, it's literally the most popular unpublished trilogy on the internet right now. I should give it a try.<br/><br/>And I regret it. I'm never again judging a book by its popularity. I honestly have no idea how the movie rights for this were bought, much less how a Big Six publishing house like Simon</span>
  <span id="freeText6551181784704954757" style="display:none">I don't normally read fan fiction on Wattpad. One Direction fanfiction, even less so. But given that this trilogy nearly has one BILLION reads altogether, I thought to myself: this can't be that bad -- after all, it's literally the most popular unpublished trilogy on the internet right now. I should give it a try.<br /><br />And I regret it. I'm never again judging a book by its popularity. I honestly have no idea how the movie rights for this were bought, much less how a Big Six publishing house like Simon &amp; Schuster actually agreed to publish it! The plot is like the other 90% of the stories on wattpad involving good girls and bad boys, only it includes the infamous Harry Styles, which is probably the only reason why it has accumulated so many views. And let me tell you, I can name at least thirty stories that are based on the same idea but are written ten times better. Yet somehow they didn't make Wattpad blow up as much as After did.<br /><br />They say that this is the new 50 shades of grey. I admit that I haven't read James' books but the situation does seem similar: 50 shades was initially a Twilight fan fiction, was it not? And this 1D fanfic is ''the next big thing'' with bidders for the movie and the publishing rights. God forbid it ever became a best seller. Books like A Proscriptive Relationship, Love at Last Sight, Late Summer Rain: that's what Wattpad's about, and that's what should be made popular by Wattpad. If After gets published with ''made popular by Wattpad'' on its front cover, I will be very disappointed because the last thing I want to see is fiction like this representing a community filled with brilliant authors.<br /><br />This, however, was so poorly written that I'm having a hard time grasping how the editor is going to make it better. Not only that, but the plot itself lacks any depth whatsoever: at least some of the similar stories I've read actually carried a message. <br /><br />This story does not. <br /><br />It is not based on love, it is based on lust. It does not portray an honest and evolving relationship. Instead, it's centered around a boy with serious anger management issues and a lovestruck girl who barely knows him but will put up with anything. The majority of the chapters consist of him abusing her emotionally and then making it all better through make up sex. It does not even follow a story line: it's chapter after chapter of the same thing.<br /><br />No. Just no. Absolutely no meaning. Absolutely no depth. Absolutely no character development. Absolutely no plot development. Absolutely nothing.<br /><br />Perhaps after its publishing it will get better. Maybe, just maybe, I'll actually bother to finish the trilogy. I would never buy this, but I would be willing to finish it on Wattpad -- although I suspect it will not get edited theре. So that's an unlikely scenario.<br /><br />But until I see a more decent version, I'll be stuck here wondering how many of the people who made this story so popular are over 13 years of age.<br /><br />(And mind you, I'd consider After 18+.)<br /><br />Sorry for being harsh. But this story does not even deserve one star in my eyes.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6551181784704954757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2863093023" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2863093023" />
    <a title="Charlotte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte"><img alt="Charlotte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487528389p2/11475773.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2863093023?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte">Charlotte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2863093023&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2863093023" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12551566713671932094">CW: abuse, sexual assault<br/><br/>Say what you will, Anna Todd is right about one thing. There is a life before and there is a life after, and once you cross that line there is no going back. Unlike Anna, however, I'm not referring to mediocre hate sex with a damaged Sad Boi™ - I'm talking about the harrowing experience of finishing this book.<br/><br/>The first thing that you have to understand about me is that I'm an awful little gremlin and I thrive when immersed in garbage. I don't know why I am the way that I</span>
  <span id="freeText12551566713671932094" style="display:none">CW: abuse, sexual assault<br /><br />Say what you will, Anna Todd is right about one thing. There is a life before and there is a life after, and once you cross that line there is no going back. Unlike Anna, however, I'm not referring to mediocre hate sex with a damaged Sad Boi™ - I'm talking about the harrowing experience of finishing this book.<br /><br />The first thing that you have to understand about me is that I'm an awful little gremlin and I thrive when immersed in garbage. I don't know why I am the way that I am, but catch me surveying my kingdom of trash upon a throne constructed from <i>My Immortal, The Room</i> and their ilk. When I heard about <i>After</i> I more or less cackled and rubbed my grimy little hands together in glee.<br /><br />I expected to be bad, and it IS bad. Everything about it is stilted, awkward and absurd. A select few of my favorite quotes, just to give you a taste of the glory:<br /><br /><i>"You're thinking about me and have that feeling...down there. Don't you, Theresa?"</i><br />Now that's what I'm talking about, babey. It's always a good sign when your sexual partner refers to your vagina as "down there!!"<br /><br /><i>"'He is such a lame,' Molly says, and I glare at her."</i><br />Presumably Tessa is glaring at her for leaving the rest of sentence hanging?<br /><br /><i>"'It's only my first semester, though so ask me again in a few months,' I joke, and everyone laughs..."</i><br />So funny!111!!!<br /><br />Mere writing mechanics aside, there's plenty to revel in. There is no plot to speak of - instead, we lurch from scene to scene of the world's most unpleasant college students stewing in sexual tension, erupting to a screaming match, agreeing to never see each other again and then doing the same thing over again the next day. As the book progresses, the conflict may also be solved with sex. The arguments will blur together. Time will no longer feel real. How did you get here? What is your name? Is it Tessa?? Hardin????<br /><br />Really, the only thing that kept me lucid was the power of my rage, because I am just as much of a feminist hag as I am a trash gremlin. Don't even try to tell me that this isn't a sick, sick relationship, or that Hardin is not an abuser. Just don't, because I have receipts:<br /><br /><i>He tosses [my notes] in the air and they fall to the ground in a scattered mess...I scramble to pick them up before he steps on them, but that's only funny to him."</i><br />Blatant disregard for damaging her personal belongings, finding humor in the other person's distress. Check. <br /><br /><i>"For a second I think he might slap me."</i><br />Fear of physical abuse when he's angry. Check. <br /><br /><i>"He drank over half the bottle! And then he started breaking things: all my mother's dishes, a glass cabinet, basically everything he could get his hands on."</i><br />Substance abuse, extreme rage, destruction of others' property and unwillingness to vent anger in any way other than destructiveness. Check.<br /><br /><i>"You are so pathetic. Don't you see that I don't want you here? I don't want you to be here for me. Just because I messed around with you doesn't mean I want anything to do with you. Yet here you are, leaving your nice boyfriend- who can actually stand to be around you- to come here and try to help me. That, Theresa, is the definition of pathetic."</i><br />Cruelty, belittlement, name calling - emotional abuse. Check. <br /><br /><i>"His hand wraps around my arm and jerks me back. 'Don't turn your back upon me!' he shouts even louder than I did."</i><br />Laying hands on your partner for the purpose of restricting their movements while angry. Check.<br /><br /><i>"But I'm cut off by his lips against mine. I push at his chest to stop him, but he doesn't budge...I feel his tongue trying to pry its way in between my lips and his strong arms wrap around me, pulling me closer to him despite my attempts to push away. It's no use; he is stronger than me."</i><br />Sexual assault. Check.<br /><br /><i>"I mean it, I don't want to see her again! And if I do, I will ruin her!"</i><br />Threats. Check.<br /><br /><i>"I get the feeling that if I don't follow he will drag me to the car."</i><br />Expectation of physical control. Check. <br /><br /><i>"'Why not? You fit in perfectly with their boring and prudish personalities.' Ouch! Why am I here again? Oh, yeah, that's right: to be Hardin's punching bag."</i><br />More cruelty and belittlement. Check.<br /><br /><i>"'You went through my phone, didn't you? You deleted the messages!' I shout at him.</i>" (He did.)<br />Extreme jealousy of other men and invasion of privacy. Check.<br /><br /><i>"I just don't like being told no."</i><br />Super normal thing to say!!!! Not at all rapey!!!! Check!!!!<br /><br /><i>"When we walk into my office Hardin grabs my wrist and turns me to face him. 'What the hell was that?' he spits out...<br />'I am sorry if you thought I was flirting with him, but I wasn't..."</i><br />This occurs after Tessa has an approximately 3 second long conversation with another dude. More extreme jealousy, possessiveness and irrational anger. Check. It's also super dope that Tessa apologizes to him. <br /><br /><i>"Then call him right now and him not to call you again."</i><br />More extreme jealousy, possessiveness and attempts to control who Tessa interacts with. Check. <br /><br />I forgot to take notes for this part, but once they move in together he essentially begins shouting at her when she asks him how his day was. <br />Irrational anger over everyday occurrences. Check. <br /><br />That's to say nothing of the fact that their entire relationship is predicated on a giant and unspeakably cruel lie and manipulation, one that makes a joke and a spectacle of Tessa's sexuality and emotions. What Hardin did to her is absolutely unforgivable, but there are like 4 more books in the series so I guarantee she's going to forgive him immediately. <br /> <br />If the point of this book was to show a deeply dysfunctional and unhealthy relationship AS SUCH, it would be one thing. I by no means think that authors should have to write only happy and healthy characters, and I believe that some of the greatest works ever written have been written about the darkest sides of humanity! BUT I believe that when you venture into the realm of abuse, sexual violence and their like, you have a responsibility to portray them accurately, respectfully and in their very real destruction and devastation.<br /><br /> <i>After</i> does not do this . If anything, the message is that the more violent and turbulent a relationship is more intense, sexy, engrossing and passionate it is. The ship has a popular hashtag, #HESSA, and a scroll through will confirm that there are readers who are genuinely invested in this relationship at face value as a romance. Tessa says that Hardin makes her feel more alive and vital, and that this is something that can never be taken away from her. <br /><br />Of course Hardin has a sad sad backstory because trauma always causes its survivors to turn abusive, that's just how psychology works!!!!! If a boy is TROUBLED and abuses a girl, it's okay!!!!! And, needless to say, he's gone to therapists before, but no one has helped him until Tessa (this is almost a literal quote from the book). NEWSFLASH: your girlfriend is not supposed to fulfill the same emotional function as a therapist! It is never a woman's job to fix a man, especially when that man is hurting her! In sum, this is not a depiction of abuse that respects the <a href="https://ncadv.org/statistics" rel="nofollow noopener">1/4</a> of women who have lived through its reality- this is a glorification of something that I don't think should ever be glorified. <br /><br />And YES, it is just fiction. But one of the main reasons I read is that fiction does not exist in a vacuum - it has so much to say about the culture that it comes from, and everything we consume has the potential to shape how we see the world. Some readers, like me, will read this for the sheer godawful spectacle, laugh and move on. Others will keep reading for the improbable happily ever after, knowing that fiction is not reality and enjoying for what it is. But what about the countless readers who originally read this on Wattpad, a website predominantly used by young teenage girls? I scrolled through the comments there, and what I saw bothered me. Some girls cooed when Hardin raised his hand at Tessa, only to lower it when he realized it was her. (As for me, I was concerned by the fact that he would be willing to hit another girl, one who he's not currently sleeping with.) Girls commented that they hoped that their first time would be like it is between Hardin and Tessa. One 10 year old on Goodreads followed me when she saw me starting to read this book, and angrily unfriended me when I started talking critically about it. <br /><br />Bottom line: I think it's a cheap excuse to say that fiction is separate from reality. Stories that promote rape myths cause increases in rape myth acceptance in their readers; stories that promote myths about abuse cause increases in acceptance of those myths just the same way. (I have empirical validation for this! I swear!) If you're grounded enough to enjoy trash for what it is and separate it from your real world values then go for it!!! I do it it too!! But I think it's important to think about the readers who haven't developed that level of critical analysis yet, and to think about the messages that these stories contribute to our broader societal discourse about sexism and violence. We already let abusers off the hook, minimize abuse and blame the victim in reality - if you're going to do these things uncritically, without commentary or subversion, in fiction then I'm sorry, but I think you are part of the problem. If I think about it for too long the existential dread hits REAL hard so uhhhhhhhh yeah. I'm gonna be done now. Time to retreat behind my unshakeable belief that My Opinion is Right. PEACE.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12551566713671932094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1149548533" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1149548533" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1149548533?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1149548533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9835291150000476454">You can go ahead and judge me for reading this, it’s okay really, I’m <br/>already judging myself for it. When I first heard of/picked up <i>After </i>and saw that it was originally 1direction fan-fiction I don’t think I’ve ever laughed so hard in my life. Then I kept seeing people post pictures and reviews on it all talking about how they are now hooked on this series. It physically hurts me to say this, but I’m hooked too. <i>After </i>is the epitome of what most would call “<i>a guilty pleasure read</i>”. <b>I have never</b></span>
  <span id="freeText9835291150000476454" style="display:none">You can go ahead and judge me for reading this, it’s okay really, I’m <br>already judging myself for it. When I first heard of/picked up <i>After </i>and saw that it was originally 1direction fan-fiction I don’t think I’ve ever laughed so hard in my life. Then I kept seeing people post pictures and reviews on it all talking about how they are now hooked on this series. It physically hurts me to say this, but I’m hooked too. <i>After </i>is the epitome of what most would call “<i>a guilty pleasure read</i>”. <b>I have never, ever hated two characters more than I hate Tessa and Hardin.</b><br><br><b>Tessa </b>is: Whiny, stuck up, annoying, childish, pathetic, a H2ho, immature, irresponsible, vapid, shallow, and an overall turd. Tessa spends 90% of this book crying and the other 10% of the time coming up with reasons to cry again.<br><br><b>Hardin </b>is: cocky, annoying, bizarre, stage five clinger, gross, <br>immature, actually a woman, hot tempered, mental, and zero dark crazy. I have no doubt in my mind that Hardin is the girl in this relationship. Trust me when I say he is more pathetic than Tessa is.<br><br>That is just the tip of the iceberg on the things I loathe about these <br>two. The relationship between the two is not only unhealthy but just <br>downright awful. It’s unbalanced and almost always one sided. Their <br>relationship is the furthest thing from romantic. Not only did I hate <br>them when they were separate but I hated them more when they were <br>together. Their relationship is way out in the deep end of the crazy pool and it was so bad I wanted to drown just trying to endure it.<br><br>As far as the plot goes, there’s not much of one. It’s just 600 pages of a rinse and repeat story line. Hardin acts like a dick, ask Tessa for <br>one more chance, Tessa says okay, they make up for a day, and then the <br>cycle starts all over again. No seriously, that’s the whole story, <br>nothing else to it. Personally, I will say that I think people are a <br>little harsh on Todd’s writing. Yes, it’s not the best, but I’ve <br>definitely seen worse. It’s just light writing. You’re never going to <br>have to Google something that is said, or have to set the book aside <br>because it gets to deep, but it’s not the worst of the worst.<br><br><i>After </i>lacks any and all originality, depth, and personality. But, you want to know what the worst part is? The downright dirty worst part?!.. Is that I couldn’t put this book down. It was like watching a car crash in slow motion. I wanted to look away but just couldn’t! And just when I think I’ll finally be able to shake the madness of this book off Anna Todd hit me hard with a WTF ending, that I didn’t see coming.<br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-8SMT9q3gTxg/VV5Yr2I5BfI/AAAAAAAABsU/tANVT1YiITM/s1600/wth.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="131" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432246474ra/14912107.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br>I hate admitting that even though I hated everything about this book, there was just something about it that kept me coming back for more.</span>

<div id="review_1159375997" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1159375997" />
    <a title="April (Aprilius Maximus)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus"><img alt="April (Aprilius Maximus)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589331862p2/20658145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1159375997?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="April (Aprilius Maximus)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="April (Aprilius Maximus)" href="/user/show/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus">April (Aprilius Maximus)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1159375997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13445123789620785596">First of all I just want to say that I was 100% ready to hate this book with a passion. I’m not a fan of Harry Styles or One Direction (haha this has since changed), but I honestly just wanted to read it so that I could form my own opinion of it and let you guys know how I felt about it.<br/><br/>I want to start off by saying that this was a Harry Styles fanfiction on wattpad that received so many views that it got published. Anna Todd has never written anything else and it’s a fanfiction, so I had to tak</span>
  <span id="freeText13445123789620785596" style="display:none">First of all I just want to say that I was 100% ready to hate this book with a passion. I’m not a fan of Harry Styles or One Direction (haha this has since changed), but I honestly just wanted to read it so that I could form my own opinion of it and let you guys know how I felt about it.<br /><br />I want to start off by saying that this was a Harry Styles fanfiction on wattpad that received so many views that it got published. Anna Todd has never written anything else and it’s a fanfiction, so I had to take that on board when I started reading it, but I was genuinely surprised. <br /><br />I understand where people are coming from when they say that Tessa and Hardin’s relationship is abusive. But I watched an interview with the author and I thought it was so interesting. She straight up said that he’s a bad person and that not all people are good. This story is realistic in that sense. Everyone has issues and he’s obviously trying to deal with those, but it’s obvious to anyone who reads this book that he’s trying so hard to change. When this is all he’s ever known, how can he just all of a sudden forget all of his past issues and be a good person? That’s just not realistic. That’s what I liked about After, that it depicted something that wasn’t necessarily good or healthy, but it was real. <br /><br />I think I may have hated this book if Tessa just took the abuse and kept crawling back to him, but she doesn’t. She sticks up for herself and is a feisty, independent character who knows what she wants, and she will tell him if he needs to get back in line and I really, really appreciated this. I don’t think this book is glamorising abusive relationships. I think it’s teaching people empathy, that not all people are perfect and how to stick up for yourself – not only did she stick up for herself to Hardin, but also to her mother.<br /><br />Going into this, I thought it would be all about the romance, but it’s not. It’s got so many other aspects in it that revolve around family, friends, university and work life. This isn’t just a love story, it’s a coming of age story. Tessa really grows as a person and realises what she wants in life and I admire that. <br /><br />Obviously this wasn’t going to be the most beautifully written book out there, but it sure was addicting and I raced through the almost 600 pages in less than 3 days. I grew to really care for these characters and want the best for them. <br /><br />Just know that I understand where the haters are coming from, but Hardin is changing for the better and is trying so hard to be good for Tessa and Tessa is a badass who can hold her own and is trying to help Hardin get over his past and become a better person. And that’s what matters, that he’s trying and that she has the compassion to help him. <br /><br />I am so surprised that I didn’t turn out to be one of the people hating on this book, and I’m so glad I gave it a chance. Don’t be embarrassed to read this book because of all of the hate it’s receiving. I say to give it a go and form your own opinion and I ask you not to judge it based on the fact that it’s a fanfiction. <br /><br />I don’t recommend this book for younger readers as there is explicit sex, swearing, drug and alcohol references and is just generally not for younger readers. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13445123789620785596" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_955031646" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/955031646" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/955031646?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

          marked it as never-ever-ever-reading-this

<div id="review_1951750638" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1951750638" />
    <a title="booksnpenguins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins"><img alt="booksnpenguins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580407796p2/66222749.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1951750638?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booksnpenguins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booksnpenguins" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins">booksnpenguins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=ya-na-contemporaries">ya-na-contemporaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=shmexy-reads">shmexy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1951750638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18228137804758486797"><i>Before you read this, please remember that this is my own personal opinion and that, with this very negative review, I'm by no means bashing those who liked this book or its characters.</i><br/><br/><a href='https://gifyu.com/image/dXXz' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586100549i/29236937._SX540_.jpg' alt='banner-di-bobi.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>That being said, I think this is the first time in my reading experience where I wish I could rate a book -5 stars. Why? Because After is the most horrible thing I've ever read in my life.<br/>It praises moral/verbal abuse and very unhealty relationships. Not to mention the slut-shaming and the way it speaks to goo</span>
  <span id="freeText18228137804758486797" style="display:none"><i>Before you read this, please remember that this is my own personal opinion and that, with this very negative review, I'm by no means bashing those who liked this book or its characters.</i><br><br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/dXXz" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586100549i/29236937._SX540_.jpg" alt="banner-di-bobi.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>That being said, I think this is the first time in my reading experience where I wish I could rate a book -5 stars. Why? Because After is the most horrible thing I've ever read in my life.<br>It praises moral/verbal abuse and very unhealty relationships. Not to mention the slut-shaming and the way it speaks to good girls as if being prude and inexperienced was something they need to fix right away. <br>I mean, I've read bad books before, and I sometimes found myself liking them or problematic characters anyway, but this? This is not problematic, not even slightly twisted. It's a straight up mess that was probably created for the sole erotic purpose but that gained a shitty plot in the making as well. <br>The main character is one of the most unrelatable girls I've ever encountered and Hardin, her male counterpart should really consider therapy or else he'd definitely nerd to be locked away. He was so scary, moody and crazy. Of course, there was the sex that should have made up for all of this, but not even all the positions of Kamasutra could save these two and their madness. <br>Also, the stereotypes killed me. In this book people were evilized or seen as bad because they have tattoos. TATTOOS, ffs.<br>The charachters are ALL incredibly fucked up and they keep making mistake after mistake. I thought there was a limit to dumbness, even in a fictional world where every single character is a failure, but apparently I was wrong. <br>Character development? Redemption? You won't find them here or in any other book of the series. <br>This story left me so uncomfortable and shaken that I had to finish a whole jar of pickles to get over it.<br>Again, if you liked it, I'm happy for you, but I will never understand how this is considered 'a masterpiece', or where it got all its success. Sometimes, fanfictions should stay fanfictions. <br>I wish I could unread it or at least forget stories as ugly as this one are being published like it's nothing, while real works of art get rejected every day.<br><br>edit Oct. 10 2019<br>I just watched the movie because it was on and I had no idea I was watching it until names were made. I kept watching it because I wanted to see if maybe it suffered from the Twilight Effect which imo made the movies more tolerable than the books (I'm still crying over that long khaki skirt) buuuuut nope. Movie adaptation not doing it for me, either.<br>I must admit that it was slightly less cringy than the books, tho, but only a bit. Those longing looks, the Truth or Dare, the peer pressure, the slut/purity-shaming and fighting were more than enough to last for weeks. <br>The actors were good and extremely pretty, so I'm giving the movie an additional quarter of a star for this! <br>And, why not, I'm also giving myself 10 gold star for the effort of not throwing my remote to the TV.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206385.png" width="80" height="80" alt="Professional Reader" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206386.png" width="80" height="80" alt="10 Book Reviews" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206384.png" width="80" height="80" alt="Reviews Published" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="18228137804758486797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2172532021" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2172532021" />
    <a title="peachygirl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51435362-peachygirl"><img alt="peachygirl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555561561p2/51435362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2172532021?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="peachygirl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="peachygirl" href="/user/show/51435362-peachygirl">peachygirl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2172532021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12723162793746656788">I read After when it was the 'It Book' on wattpad a few years back and I'm embarrassed to admit that I read all the 3 books in the series (the original one before Ms.Todd decided to milk this for all it's worth and came up with more unnecessary drama in an already fucked up relationship). In my defense, I wanted to see if the girl would grow some balls and dump Harry's sorry ass, which does happen time and again, till Harry strips and Tessa falls head over heels in lust. Needless to say I was re</span>
  <span id="freeText12723162793746656788" style="display:none">I read After when it was the 'It Book' on wattpad a few years back and I'm embarrassed to admit that I read all the 3 books in the series (the original one before Ms.Todd decided to milk this for all it's worth and came up with more unnecessary drama in an already fucked up relationship). In my defense, I wanted to see if the girl would grow some balls and dump Harry's sorry ass, which does happen time and again, till Harry strips and Tessa falls head over heels in lust. Needless to say I was repulsed.<br /><br />The girl in me hated the character Harry/Hardin. But the reader in me was furious with the way the author romanticised every red flag and abuse. <br /><br />Still I suffered 300 chapters in the hope of redemption or closure or anything to make me believe I hadn't wasted time on these books, but it was a hopeless cause. So being the mature person that I am (erm, sometimes), I tried to forget I ever read such a shitty piece of literature and moved on.<br /><br />I wouldn't have wasted more time on writing this review if it weren't for a friend of mine who said she wanted a boyfriend like Harry/Hardin. I was stumped and gave her a 40 minute lecture, which ended with me being called a grandma.(!!)<br /><br />If anyone's reading this, come out of your After ever happy bubble and smell the fucking coffee. Try to understand that what Hardin and Tessa had was not love. Or the kind of relationship you would want to aspire for. It was a disproportionate mess of lies, games, manipulation, emotional abuse, unhealthy attachments, unresolved mental issues and lots of sex! <br />And I'm still trying to wrap my mind around the fact that this book is a bestseller (and now, a movie deal?!) <br />Just what the heck is wrong with everyone??</span>
  <a data-text-id="12723162793746656788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1509588367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1509588367" />
    <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli"><img alt="Pearl Angeli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588420465p2/31514572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1509588367?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=new-adult-contemporary">new-adult-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=annoying-heroines">annoying-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=smexy-read">smexy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=hot-male-characters">hot-male-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=rants">rants</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1509588367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17932691819007724202"><b>First DNF book of the year.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430373928ra/14708012.gif' width='360' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>One of the things I hate doing so much is DNF-ing a book because it feels bad to leave it when you've invested yourself in it in the first place. But sometimes you just have to quit because it just doesn't work out for you. And you can no longer fool yourself and hope that things will get better as the story goes.<br/><br/>So yeah.. I DNF-ed this book for these reasons:<br/><br/>1. <b>Writing Style</b> - This book is poorly written and executed. I see so much potentials in this book but it fails</span>
  <span id="freeText17932691819007724202" style="display:none"><b>First DNF book of the year.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430373928ra/14708012.gif" width="360" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One of the things I hate doing so much is DNF-ing a book because it feels bad to leave it when you've invested yourself in it in the first place. But sometimes you just have to quit because it just doesn't work out for you. And you can no longer fool yourself and hope that things will get better as the story goes.<br><br>So yeah.. I DNF-ed this book for these reasons:<br><br>1. <b>Writing Style</b> - This book is poorly written and executed. I see so much potentials in this book but it fails to hold my attention most of the time because of the boring writing.<br><br>2. <b>Plot</b> - You can never find an absolute plot in this book. Every chapter is a complete waste because of so many unnecessary scenes that don't make any sense at all.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445837983ra/16709229.gif" width="350" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>3. <b>Main Characters</b> - If you can't love the main characters, then there's no reason to continue it. Why pretend and fool yourself? Tessa and Hardin are both immature characters. They always bicker like children and wow, their childish behavior annoys the crap out of me! And don't even get me started on Hardin's attitude! Gaaah this guy makes me want to pull my hair out because he's simply such a prick! <br><br>4. <b>Cheating</b> - Just so we're clear, I despise books with cheating, but I admit that there are books that I loved even when there's cheating involved but that's because they're simply well-written and well-justified. But this? A girl cheats on her boyfriend just because her boyfriend is boring and omg there's a tattooed and pierced boy-next-door who's way hotter and exciting than him. What the actual f*ck? And damn Hardin. This guy! He knows the girl has a boyfriend and yet he continues to seduce her just so he can prove that he's a sex god!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453091776ra/17779860.gif" width="350" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453091776ra/17779861.gif" width="320" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I did try to like this book, honestly. But I just can't. It was a waste of time. Nuff said.</span>

After, book 1 of 5. The unlikely against-all-odds romance between tatted rebel Hardin Scott &amp; good girl Tessa Young!</b><br><br><a>

</a><br><u>Books in The After series should be read in order:</u><br><b>Book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1090449623" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">After</a><br>Book 2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1952340915" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">After We Collided</a><br>Book 3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1994022284" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">After We Fell</a><br>Book 4: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2000467437" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">After Ever Happy</a><br>Book 5: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2000467456" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Before</a></b><br><br>The After series is the epic love saga between flawed rebel bad boy student and editor <b>Hardin Allen Scott</b> and naïve good girl student and intern editor <b>Theresa Lynn Young, Tessa.</b><br><br>After, book 1 follows Hardin and Tessa from an <b>unlikely friendship</b> and beyond. Their, at times, <b>tumultuous</b> relationship will be tested with demons from their pasts, jealousy, secrets, lies and betrayal. <br><br>Yet their biggest obstacles will always come from within. It’s their journey of <b>self-discovery, testing boundaries, pushing limits</b> and <b>surrendering</b> it all for love.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496016874ra/22874859.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Nine words to describe <b> Hardin Allen Scott:</b> Unpredictable, moody, flawed, broken, aloof, secretive, demanding, conflicted and possessive.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496016874ra/22874860.gif" width="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Nine words to describe <b> Theresa Lynn Young, Tessa:</b> Organized, meek, compulsive, goal-oriented, determined, naïve, trusting, curious and forgiving.<br><br><b>After</b> is told from Tessa’s POV, but next-coming books will be dual. It’s an <b>unlikely, all-consuming, addicting,</b> at times angsty love story between two polar opposites. It ends shockingly with truth and understanding leading right to book 2, <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1952340915" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">After We Collided</a>
</b> for the <b>continuation</b> of their journey.<br><br><a>

<div id="review_1085549251" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1085549251" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1085549251?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22813719-after">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=shocking-twists">shocking-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=hate-that-i-love-them">hate-that-i-love-them</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=tearjerkers">tearjerkers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1085549251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5000884389759463137">If you thought the 'Fallen Crest High' series was full of angst and teenage melodrama, you haven't seen anything yet! 'After' is like many other teenage/college-aged romances, with all the "end of the world" dramatics...on steroids. I found this book to be equal parts irritating and addicting. <br/><br/>The "adult" part of me has to acknowledge the truth in much of the criticism I've seen regarding this story. Hardin and Tessa's relationship was a train wreck. I spent a lot of time rolling my eyes and thi</span>
  <span id="freeText5000884389759463137" style="display:none">If you thought the 'Fallen Crest High' series was full of angst and teenage melodrama, you haven't seen anything yet! 'After' is like many other teenage/college-aged romances, with all the "end of the world" dramatics...on steroids. I found this book to be equal parts irritating and addicting. <br /><br />The "adult" part of me has to acknowledge the truth in much of the criticism I've seen regarding this story. Hardin and Tessa's relationship was a train wreck. I spent a lot of time rolling my eyes and thinking "hang it up already". However, I'd be lying if I said that I didn't enjoy this story. It was a total guilty pleasure. Even though I was often annoyed, or even infuriated, by the goings on in this book, I couldn't turn away. I really enjoyed this book, despite the responsible adult in me saying I should run far in the other direction.<br /><br />The story centers on Theresa "Tessa" Young and her relationship with Hardin Scott. Tessa is portrayed as the quintessential sheltered prude. She is a sweet virgin, who dresses conservatively and arrives at her dorm with her over-bearing mother and high school sweetheart in-tow. Immediately, Tessa stands out and becomes a target for her roommate's hard-partying group of friends. <br /><br />More so than anyone else, Hardin seems to take extreme pleasure in tormenting Tessa. He is constantly toying with her and trying to humiliate her. He goes out of his way to put her down, but he's always there. Despite all of his insults, he is constantly showing up in her daily life. <br /><br />Little by little, Tessa and Hardin form a tenuous friendship. Eventually, it grows into more. There are plenty of obstacles along the way -- none larger than Hardin's broody, closed-off, and often volatile nature. Time and time again, Tessa forgives Hardin for his reprehensible behavior. <br /><br />These two might take the prize for the number of times a single couple can go back and forth, breaking up and making up, in a single book. It did start to wear on my nerves, even as I couldn't turn away. They were the perfect example of everything that only works in fiction. In real life, these two needed some serious counselling and intervention. They were toxic, to an extreme degree. No way would I ever want to be any where near a couple like this in real life. However, for a smutty romance, they definitely kept things interesting. <br /><br />While I don't want to give anything away, I will say that the ending of this book gutted me. I actually cried. I was so furious, I think I might have felt the betrayal as acutely as Tessa did! <br /><br />So many times, I told myself that when this book was over that I wouldn't be diving back in for another round of their melodramatic, childish antics. I was kidding myself. There was no way that I was going to skip the next book after that ending. It's on to the next book for me. <br /><br />As an aside, this book was apparently written as fan-fiction originally. It is supposed to be based on the lives of the boy band "One Direction". Since I'm not very familiar with this group, I don't have anything to offer in terms of how closely this book follows any of those band members. If it does closely follow one of the bandmate's lives, God help the poor girls that are his prey.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5000884389759463137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9563600666442884592"><b>everyone:</b> omg. a wattpad fanfic of harry styles got published AND turned into a movie!? fdlafkjdlakdakjsl.<br/><br/><b>me, an intellectual:</b> niall is actually the best member of one direction and thats a fact.<br/>____________________________________<br/><br/>my boyband preferences (and truth) aside, i really dont know what to say about this. it was... well, it just was. <br/><br/>can i see why its so hated? absolutely. this is one of the most toxic relationships (real or fictional) i have ever seen. i have no respect for either MC a</span>
  <span id="freeText9563600666442884592" style="display:none"><b>everyone:</b> omg. a wattpad fanfic of harry styles got published AND turned into a movie!? fdlafkjdlakdakjsl.<br /><br /><b>me, an intellectual:</b> niall is actually the best member of one direction and thats a fact.<br />____________________________________<br /><br />my boyband preferences (and truth) aside, i really dont know what to say about this. it was... well, it just was. <br /><br />can i see why its so hated? absolutely. this is one of the most toxic relationships (real or fictional) i have ever seen. i have no respect for either MC and they are both beyond frustrating. harry styles should be livid that hardin is inspired by him. also, the writing just straight up sucks. i get that its fanfic, but at least edit it before its published.<br /><br />can i also understand why people say its a page turner? you betcha. i was constantly hooked, wondering how the heck hardin and tessa were ever going to work it out. also, that ending!! holy crap. that was one of the hardest things i have ever had to read. i never knew i could experience so much secondhand humiliation and heartbreak. <br /><br />so i get everything everyone has been saying. i agree with both the 1 and 5 star reviews. so im gonna put my rating right in the middle for now. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>2.5 stars</i></b></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3591636119" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1119504182783465953">"Fifty Shades of Grey glorifies toxic and abusive relationships."<br/><b>After: </b> Hold my beer <br/><br/>It's okay to cheat on someone if you lose interest in them. It's okay to choose an abusive, toxic relationship over a real and a healthy one. It's okay to slut-shame anyone whenever you feel like it. <br/>Simply amazing. <br/><br/><br/><br/></span>

<div id="review_2049770194" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2049770194" />
    <a title="Karen Mc " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11017760-karen-mc"><img alt="Karen Mc " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589665192p2/11017760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2049770194?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen Mc " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen Mc " href="/user/show/11017760-karen-mc">Karen Mc </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11017760-karen-mc?shelf=angst">angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11017760-karen-mc?shelf=college">college</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2049770194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17125088273996526256"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1484234393p8/1801286.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Sometimes you read a story that strikes you hard where you're drifting in the haze left from characters who clenched every part of you. <i>After</i> by Anna Todd rendered me SPEECHLESS for the first time ever after finishing a book. I was left in a DAZE, my mind SPINNING. My heart pounded fast like drums in my chest. I was struck so hard by this TORNADO of a TALE that twisted and turned my heart so many times that I could barely breathe. <b><i>After</i> removed me from everything where I did nothing but LIVE thi</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17125088273996526256" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1484234393p8/1801286.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sometimes you read a story that strikes you hard where you're drifting in the haze left from characters who clenched every part of you. <i>After</i> by Anna Todd rendered me SPEECHLESS for the first time ever after finishing a book. I was left in a DAZE, my mind SPINNING. My heart pounded fast like drums in my chest. I was struck so hard by this TORNADO of a TALE that twisted and turned my heart so many times that I could barely breathe. <b><i>After</i> removed me from everything where I did nothing but LIVE this book.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499647728ra/23254707.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>After</i> started out slow but a burn built that beckoned me right into the flames as my heart caught fire, a slow burn seeping into my soul. My emotions were heightened, swirling around in my head like a hurricane, waiting to hit. My feels flooded…all over me. <b><i>After</i> is thigh-clenching, adrenaline-inducing, emotional-exploding edge-of-your-seat exhilaration in words.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1499646382p8/3601048.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Tess is a beautiful and innocent...a good girl. Her focus is on school and she doesn't need any distractions, even if it's the beautiful disaster of a bad boy named Hardin.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Hardin is like a drug; each time I take the tiniest bite of him, I crave more and more.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><b><i>After</i> was MY DRUG and I CRAVED this story the more I read...like air needed to breathe.</b><br><br>Hardin is my favorite type of hero: a hot, inked, cocky, built, and broken alpha. I loved him. I hated him. Often, I didn't know how I felt about this devastatingly beautiful but mixed-up man. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>I am a moth to his flame, and he never hesitates to burn me.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><b>Tess and Hardins' story was my FIRE with flames that blazed and burned...DETONATING ME.</b> The chemistry between Tess and Hardin, polar opposites in looks but kindred souls, is COMBUSTIBLE. Hardin is smoldering inked perfection, a man who commands, where you can only succumb to the desire. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Do you want me fingers or my tongue?" he whispers seductively.<br><br>"Both."<br><br>"As you wish."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Oh did Hardin's words POSSESS ME. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>He makes me laugh and cry, yell and scream, but most of all he makes me feel alive.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><b><i>After</i>, this EXHILARATION in words, made me feel ALIVE.</b><br><br>Tess...this heroine gains more strength with the turn of each page. This heroine grows up so much in this story. I wanted to high-five her a few times for standing up for herself. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"You...you make me want to be good, for you...I want to be good for you, Tess."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>These words, so PASSIONATE and POIGNANT, MELTED ME. <br><br>Tess and Hardin are fire and ice. The push and pull between them is PALPABLE. I both loathed and loved Tess and Hardin together. I wanted to both hug and hit some much-needed sense into them. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"You promised you wouldn't ruin me."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Just WOW!!! I was WRECKED!!! My kindle almost didn't survive this story and neither did I. <b>Anna Todd's <i>After</i> RUINED me!!! <i>After</i> is DEVASTATINGLY BEAUTIFUL. This book is bittersweet and broken love at its best.</b><br><br>Anna Todd is my newest LITERARY HERO!!! Her words are LIFE!!! <b>Anna Todd delivers ALL THE ANGST in <i>After</i> that makes you FEEL ALL THE FEELS!!!</b> Oh did I feel every word in <i>After</i> where I was a PRISONER to its words.<br><br><i>After</i> was my HIGH...its angst my ADRENALINE and ADDICTION. I smiled ... swooned ... cried ... frowned ...sighed ... and wanted to gut-punch a character or two. This ROLLER COASTER of a ROMANCE was my RUSH, this riveting ride in words, where I could do nothing except hold on tight as my soul soared and shattered so many times. <b>This book BROKE ME IN THE BEST WAY!!!</b><br><br><b><i>After</i> crashed into me with a force I never saw coming, one where I COULD ONLY FEEL, which made me splendidly succumb to this story over and over again.</b> I not only LOVED THIS angst-ridden love story, <i>After</i>, I NEEDED IT!!! I CRAVED this book that is angst and adrenaline meets POWER and PASSION. <i>After</i> was my DRUG and I need more, as one hit was not enough.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>If I could only feel one thing for the rest of my life, this would be it.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟 <b>'but worth all of the' soul-slaying stars</b><br><br>A Top 2017 MUST-MEET ROMANCE!!! <br><br>▶️ <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/2tQWIpm">http://amzn.to/2tQWIpm</a> ◀️<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1484235311p8/1801294.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Web</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookaliciousbabes.com">http://www.bookaliciousbabes.com</a><br><b>Facebook</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/bookaliciousbabesblog">http://www.facebook.com/bookaliciousb...</a><br><b>Readers Group</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/groups/BBBBookPimps">http://www.facebook.com/groups/BBBBoo...</a> <br><b>Twitter</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.twitter.com/bookaliciousbb">http://www.twitter.com/bookaliciousbb</a><br><b>Instagram</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.instagram.com/bookaliciousbb">http://www.instagram.com/bookaliciousbb</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17125088273996526256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2075708325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11323951617637673390">This was my first buddy read along with my girls Mareira and Maria Vrisanaki. I have to thank those two amazing ladies who made the experience unique and one of the funniest in my life! Even though the book was quite terrible, they made me laugh and enjoy the whole process.<br/><br/>I have to admit that the first impression of the story was a positive one. Although, I knew that the first impressions aren't always accurate, I didn't even think about it. I was too into the story and the love interest betwee</span>
  <span id="freeText11323951617637673390" style="display:none">This was my first buddy read along with my girls Mareira and Maria Vrisanaki. I have to thank those two amazing ladies who made the experience unique and one of the funniest in my life! Even though the book was quite terrible, they made me laugh and enjoy the whole process.<br><br>I have to admit that the first impression of the story was a positive one. Although, I knew that the first impressions aren't always accurate, I didn't even think about it. I was too into the story and the love interest between these two completely different personalities. Furthermore, it was an easy and fast-paced read and I could relate myself to the main character, Tess. She's described as a very organised young woman who had studied and sacrificed a lot to get into a dignified college. My inner voice was screaming: "YAAAS! It is the perfect summer read". If only I knew... <br><br>After I've read the first half of the book I couldn't hide anymore my annoyance due to the childish behaviour of the two protagonists. I had supposed that Tess, would prove a mature young lady, since she was presented as an independent and self-sufficient character. Moreover, her reading preferences, which included "Wuthering Heights" and "Pride and Prejudice" implied the presence of a mature personality, able to think and analyze every situation deeply as well as to cherish her uniqueness and her morals. I was very disappointed by the absence of the above. Besides, I only saw a regression in her behaviour and her believes. She wasn't even able to stand for herself or to rely on her knowledge and qualifications to gain an internship. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515927197ra/24874101.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Hardin, Tess' love interest, was presented to the readers as a rude and a badass personage. The author keeps this consistent pattern throughout the story. There are some points where she tries to justify his behaviour and gives us the illusion that we can understand him. As a result, we begin to think that he has actually changed. Until the very end when the writer introduces her main plot twist. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515927197ra/24874099.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anna Todd uses a poor vocabulary and her writing style would characterised as a mediocre one. The language is repetitive and a little bit boring. <br><br>The most important here is to emphasise the message that she wanted to pass. Wait. . . a what? She forgot about this little and significant detail that every book has to contain. <br><br>I better have to put it in another way. She somehow manages to pass all the wrong messages. Unfortunately, the story shows clearly that we don't have to embrace the difference but to be afraid of it. What is more, she insist clearly that there is no such concept as friendship between people who are "different". Finally, throughout the book she presents that women are nothing more than foolish, weak-willed and inefficient creatures. Sounds terrible? It is terrible!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515927197ra/24874100.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All in all, if you are searching for your next funny, easy with a decent message read, this book is not for you. On the other hand, if you are in the mood to read a "50 Shades of Grey" related story, this one is the best solution.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11323951617637673390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tCaAtftN6RngNJ40KfFEbtAmgqhY8Iaf8V42KFZF7mvyDpeoOjQ6aLA1sS2/Wkic6GlDKQAm/riJTMf1IJs3fQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GGDC17xCRBWN6bsMYDidXyXqVNElvUTwGaX0uYKyE9FeSNXKfTuXZN3olBX2k5GtHaWVUH1rPNdhtwVk9GzKxw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer2300446274373957645">ANNA TODD (Author/Writer/Producer) is the New York Times bestselling author of the After series of books, The Spring Girls, and the recent The Brightest Stars.<br/> <br/>Always an avid reader, Todd began writing stories on her phone on Wattpad, the reading and writing multiplatform for original stories, with After becoming its most-read series with over 1.5 billion reads. <br/> <br/>The print edition of After was pub</span>
  <span id="freeText2300446274373957645" style="display:none">ANNA TODD (Author/Writer/Producer) is the New York Times bestselling author of the After series of books, The Spring Girls, and the recent The Brightest Stars.<br /> <br />Always an avid reader, Todd began writing stories on her phone on Wattpad, the reading and writing multiplatform for original stories, with After becoming its most-read series with over 1.5 billion reads. <br /> <br />The print edition of After was published in 2014 by Simon &amp; Schuster and has since been released in over 30 languages with more than 11 million copies sold worldwide. After has been a #1 bestseller across the globe including Italy, Germany, France and Spain. She has since written eight additional novels and serves as a producer and screenwriter on the upcoming film adaptation of After We Collided, the sequel to After. <br /> <br />Todd has been hailed by Cosmopolitan as “the biggest literary phenomenon of her generation.” A native of Ohio Anna, her husband and son currently live in Los Angeles.<br /> <br />Find her at AnnaTodd.com, on Twitter at @annatodd, on Instagram at @annatodd, and on Wattpad as Imaginator1D.<br /><br />Sign up for her mailing list for all the latest news: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://eepurl.com/cEm5e9">http://eepurl.com/cEm5e9</a><br />For more information on Anna Todd visit her website: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.annatodd.com/">http://www.annatodd.com/</a></span>
